## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (deterministic rate laws / concentration ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard modeling object in chemical reaction kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are phenomenological rate laws dA_dt = f(A) and possibly time-varying-rate effects dA_dt = f(t, A) (e.g., catalyst decay, driving/feeding, or changing conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate source/sink over time)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular growth/decay; c0<0 for decay)
- Second-order (self-reaction): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular depletion or autocombination-like kinetics)
- General n-th order power law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order not necessarily integer)
- Reversible first-order toward equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (relaxation toward steady concentration c1)
- Logistic/autocatalytic with carrying limit: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-enhancing growth with depletion/limitation)
- Autocatalysis with baseline term: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (mixture of linear and quadratic pathways)
- Cubic/quenching term: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**3 (growth at low A with high-A suppression)
- Rational inhibition (substrate/product inhibition surrogate): dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate increases then levels off due to limited reactive capacity)
- Rational negative feedback: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) - c2 * A (net effect of saturating production and linear loss)
- Time-dependent rate constant (exponential drift): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (changing conditions or catalyst activation/deactivation modeled via k(t))
- Time-dependent rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (slowly varying effective rate, e.g., ramped conditions)
- Periodic forcing of rate: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally driven modulation, e.g., light-driven/periodic feed effects)
- Forced relaxation with time-varying setpoint: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 + c2 * t - A) (tracking a drifting equilibrium/target concentration)
- Additive source plus decay: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant inflow/formation with first-order removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: if doubling A roughly doubles dA_dt → linear term c0*A; if it quadruples → quadratic term c0*A**2; non-integer scaling suggests c0*A**c1.
- Approach-to-equilibrium behavior: if dA_dt changes sign at a particular A and trends toward that point, use a restoring form c0*(c1 - A) or include multiple fixed points via polynomials.
- Positivity/physical bounds: concentration A should remain nonnegative; rate laws often include factors of A (so dA_dt → 0 as A → 0) or stable fixed points at A=0.
- Autocatalysis signature: accelerating change with increasing A at low/moderate A suggests superlinear dependence (A**2, A*(c1-A), or mixed A + A**2).
- Inhibition/limited capacity: if dA_dt increases with A then plateaus, prefer saturating rational structures like c0*A/(A+c1) rather than unbounded polynomials.
- Competing pathways: curvature that cannot be captured by a single order often indicates sums of mechanisms (e.g., c0*A + c1*A**2) with different dominance regimes.
- Time-varying conditions: if dA_dt at the same A differs systematically across t, include k(t) modulation (c0 + c1*t, exp(c*t), or sinusoidal forcing) multiplying A or (c1-A).
- Steady production plus removal: if dA_dt is positive at A≈0 but becomes negative at large A, a source–sink balance c0 - c1*A (or higher-order sink) is a natural structure.
- Multiple steady states: S-shaped dA_dt vs A (three zeros) suggests cubic-like kinetics (e.g., c0*A - c1*A**3) or polynomial mixtures rather than single-order laws.

So any matching candidate must (i) have exactly one \(t\)-dependent term of the form \(A\cdot(\text{const})\cdot e^{(\text{const})t}\) with negative exponent coefficient \(-0.0816...\), (ii) have an \(A\)-only oscillatory term equal to \(0.84034...\cos(\log(A+1))\), and (iii) have no extra \(A\)-only terms (polynomials, logs, abs, etc.) unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Also note: many candidates use \(\sin(c7\log(\cdot)+c9)\). This can represent a cosine via phase shift: \(\sin(x+\pi/2)=\cos(x)\). And \(\log(A*c+1)\) can match \(\log(A+1)\) only if \(c=1\). Any use of \(\log(c\lvert A\rvert+1)\), \(\Max(0,A)\), \(\Abs(A)\), \(\sqrt{\cdot}\), rational terms, etc. generally cannot equal \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) for all real \(A\) (and even for all \(A>-1\)) unless those parts are zeroed out.

- \(c0=0\), \(c4=0\), \(c5=0\).
All terms then match exactly. **Yes, match possible**.

The third term is `exp(c7*cos(...))`, not `cos(...)`. These are fundamentally different — exp of cos cannot equal cos. **No match.**
